<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Green_politics" title="Template:Green politics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

</table>
<p><b>Eco-socialism</b>, <b>green socialism</b> or <b>socialist ecology</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Ideology" title="Ideology">ideology</a> merging aspects of <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> with that of <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">green politics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alter-globalization" title="Alter-globalization">alter-globalization</a> or <a href="/wiki/Anti-globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-globalization">anti-globalization</a>. Eco-socialists generally believe that the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> system is the cause of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>, <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a> through <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a>, under the supervision of repressive <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">states</a> and transnational structures.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Eco-socialists advocate dismantling capitalism, focusing on <a href="/wiki/Common_ownership" title="Common ownership">common ownership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> by freely associated producers, and restoring the <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Lucas" title="Caroline Lucas">Caroline Lucas</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party of England and Wales</a>, has described her party's brand of socialism as appealing to both middle-class environmentalists as well as working-class socialists.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology">Ideology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Ideology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eco-socialists are critical of many past and existing forms of both <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green politics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>. They are often described as "<a href="/wiki/Red_(political_adjective)" class="mw-redirect" title="Red (political adjective)">Red</a> Greens" - adherents to Green politics with clear <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a> views, often inspired by <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> (Red Greens are in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Eco-capitalism" title="Eco-capitalism">eco-capitalists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Green_anarchism" title="Green anarchism">Green anarchists</a>).</p>
<p>The term "watermelon" is commonly applied, often pejoratively, to <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Greens</a> who seem to put "<a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>" goals above <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> ones, implying they are "green on the outside but red on the inside"; the term is usually attributed to either <a href="/wiki/Petr_Beckmann" title="Petr Beckmann">Petr Beckmann</a> or, more frequently, <a href="/wiki/Warren_T._Brookes" title="Warren T. Brookes">Warren T. Brookes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-RatsNestWatermelon_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RatsNestWatermelon-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NoWatermelonBlog_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NoWatermelonBlog-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheAmericanSpectator_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheAmericanSpectator-5">[5]</a></sup> both critics of <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>, and is common in Australia,<sup id="cite_ref-AustrailianWatermelon_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AustrailianWatermelon-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AustrailianWatermelon2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AustrailianWatermelon2-7">[7]</a></sup> New Zealand<sup id="cite_ref-WatermelonNZ_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WatermelonNZ-8">[8]</a></sup> and the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Frontpage_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontpage-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>A New Zealand website, <i>The Watermelon</i>, uses the term proudly, stating that it is "green on the outside and <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">liberal</a> on the inside", while also citing "socialist political leanings", reflecting the use of the term "liberal" to describe the <a href="/wiki/Left_wing" class="mw-redirect" title="Left wing">left wing</a> in many English-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-WatermelonNZ_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WatermelonNZ-8">[8]</a></sup> Red Greens are often considered "<a href="/wiki/Fundi_(politics)" title="Fundi (politics)">fundies</a>" or "fundamentalist greens", a term usually associated with <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">Deep Ecology</a> even though the <a href="/wiki/German_Green_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="German Green Party">German Green Party</a> "fundi" faction included eco-socialists, and eco-socialists in other <a href="/wiki/Green_Parties" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Parties">Green Parties</a>, like <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Derek Wall</a>, have been described in the press as fundies.<sup id="cite_ref-Mail21Sep_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mail21Sep-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LynasBlog_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LynasBlog-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eco-socialists also criticise bureaucratic and elite theories of self-described socialism such as <a href="/wiki/Maoism" title="Maoism">Maoism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a> and what other critics have termed <a href="/wiki/Bureaucratic_collectivism" title="Bureaucratic collectivism">bureaucratic collectivism</a> or <a href="/wiki/State_capitalism" title="State capitalism">state capitalism</a>. Instead, eco-socialists focus on imbuing socialism with ecology while keeping the emancipatory goals of "first-epoch" socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Eco-socialists aim for communal ownership of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> by "freely associated producers" with all forms of domination eclipsed, especially <a href="/wiki/Ecofeminism" title="Ecofeminism">gender inequality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>This often includes the restoration of <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a> land in opposition to <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Guha_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guha-12">[12]</a></sup> in which local control of resources valorizes the Marxist concept of <a href="/wiki/Use_value" title="Use value">use value</a> above <a href="/wiki/Exchange_value" title="Exchange value">exchange value</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Practically, eco-socialists have generated various strategies to mobilise action on an <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">internationalist</a> basis, developing networks of grassroots individuals and groups that can radically transform society through <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">nonviolent</a> "prefigurative projects" for a <a href="/wiki/Post-capitalism" title="Post-capitalism">post-capitalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-statism" title="Anti-statism">post-statist</a> world.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1880s.E2.80.931930s_.E2.80.93_Marx.2C_Morris_and_influence_on_the_Russian_Revolution">1880s–1930s – Marx, Morris and influence on the Russian Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1880s–1930s – Marx, Morris and influence on the Russian Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Contrary to the depiction of <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> by some environmentalists,<sup id="cite_ref-Eckersley_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eckersley-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Social_ecology" title="Social ecology">social ecologists</a><sup id="cite_ref-Clark_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clark-15">[15]</a></sup> and fellow <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialists</a><sup id="cite_ref-Benton_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton-16">[16]</a></sup> as a <a href="/wiki/Productivism" title="Productivism">productivist</a> who favoured the domination of nature, eco-socialists have revisited Marx's writings and believe that he "was a main originator of the <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> world-view".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Eco-socialist authors, like <a href="/wiki/John_Bellamy_Foster" title="John Bellamy Foster">John Bellamy Foster</a><sup id="cite_ref-JBF_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JBF-17">[17]</a></sup> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Burkett&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paul Burkett (page does not exist)">Paul Burkett</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Burkett_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkett-18">[18]</a></sup> point to Marx's discussion of a "metabolic rift" between man and nature, his statement that "private ownership of the globe by single individuals will appear quite absurd as private ownership of one man by another" and his observation that a society must "hand it [the planet] down to succeeding generations in an improved condition".<sup id="cite_ref-Capital3_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capital3-19">[19]</a></sup> Nonetheless, other eco-socialists feel that Marx overlooked a "recognition of nature in and for itself", ignoring its "receptivity" and treating nature as "subjected to labor from the start" in an "entirely active relationship".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Therefore, <a href="/wiki/William_Morris" title="William Morris">William Morris</a>, the <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> novelist, poet and designer, is largely credited with developing key principles of what was later called eco-socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup> During the 1880s and 1890s, Morris promoted his eco-socialist ideas within the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Federation" title="Social Democratic Federation">Social Democratic Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialist_League_(UK,_1885)" title="Socialist League (UK, 1885)">Socialist League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GLSite_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GLSite-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_(1917)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution (1917)">Russian Revolution</a>, some <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_science" title="Environmental science">environmental scientists</a> attempted to integrate <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> consciousness into <a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevism">Bolshevism</a>, although many such people were later purged from the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gare_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gare-22">[22]</a></sup> The "pre-revolutionary environmental movement", encouraged by revolutionary scientist <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Bogdanov" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksandr Bogdanov">Aleksandr Bogdanov</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Proletkult" title="Proletkult">Proletkul't</a> organisation, made efforts to "integrate production with natural laws and limits" in the first decade of Soviet rule, before <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> attacked ecologists and the science of ecology and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> fell into the <a href="/wiki/Pseudo-science" class="mw-redirect" title="Pseudo-science">pseudo-science</a> of the state biologist <a href="/wiki/Trofim_Lysenko" title="Trofim Lysenko">Trofim Lysenko</a>, who "set about to rearrange the Russian map" in ignorance of environmental limits.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecoanarchism">Ecoanarchism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ecoanarchism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Green_anarchism" title="Template:Green anarchism"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Template_talk:Green_anarchism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Template talk:Green anarchism (page does not exist)"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>

<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Green_anarchism" title="Green anarchism">Green anarchism</a></div>
<p>Green anarchism, or ecoanarchism, is a <a href="/wiki/Anarchist_schools_of_thought" title="Anarchist schools of thought">school of thought</a> within <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a> which puts a particular emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental issues">environmental issues</a>. An important early influence was the thought of the American <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a> and his book <i><a href="/wiki/Walden" title="Walden">Walden</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Thoreau_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thoreau-23">[23]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Leo_Tolstoy" title="Leo Tolstoy">Leo Tolstoy</a><sup id="cite_ref-naturismolibertario_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naturismolibertario-24">[24]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Elisee_Reclus" class="mw-redirect" title="Elisee Reclus">Elisee Reclus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reclus1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reclus1-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In the late 19th century there emerged <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-naturism" title="Anarcho-naturism">anarcho-naturism</a> as the fusion of anarchism and <a href="/wiki/Naturism" title="Naturism">naturist</a> philosophies within <a href="/wiki/Individualist_anarchist" class="mw-redirect" title="Individualist anarchist">individualist anarchist</a> circles in France, Spain, Cuba<sup id="cite_ref-raforum.info_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-raforum.info-27">[27]</a></sup> and Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-naturismolibertario_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naturismolibertario-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spanishind_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spanishind-28">[28]</a></sup> Several anarchists from the mid-20th century, including <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Read" title="Herbert Read">Herbert Read</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethel_Mannin" title="Ethel Mannin">Ethel Mannin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Kohr" title="Leopold Kohr">Leopold Kohr</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Sale-foreward_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-foreward-29">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Ellul" title="Jacques Ellul">Jacques Ellul</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Goodman_(writer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Goodman (writer)">Paul Goodman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-rg_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-31">[31]</a></sup> also held proto-environmental views linked to their anarchism. Mannin's 1944 book <i>Bread and Roses: A Utopian Survey and Blue-Print</i> has been described by anarchist historian <a href="/wiki/Robert_Graham_(historian)" title="Robert Graham (historian)">Robert Graham</a> as setting forth "an <a href="/wiki/Ecological" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecological">ecological</a> vision in opposition to the prevailing and destructive <a href="/wiki/Industrial_society" title="Industrial society">industrial</a> organization of society".<sup id="cite_ref-rg_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-31">[31]</a></sup> Important contemporary currents are <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">anarcho-primitivism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_ecology" title="Social ecology">social ecology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_ecology_and_communalism">Social ecology and communalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Social ecology and communalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Social_ecology" title="Social ecology">Social ecology</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communalism_(Political_Philosophy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Communalism (Political Philosophy)">Communalism (Political Philosophy)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Murray_Bookchin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Murray_Bookchin.jpg/200px-Murray_Bookchin.jpg" width="200" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Murray_Bookchin.jpg/300px-Murray_Bookchin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Murray_Bookchin.jpg/400px-Murray_Bookchin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3429" data-file-height="4286" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Murray_Bookchin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Social ecology is closely related to the work and ideas of <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a> and influenced by anarchist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a>. Social ecologists assert that the present <a href="/wiki/Ecological_crisis" title="Ecological crisis">ecological crisis</a> has its roots in human social problems, and that the domination of human-over-nature stems from the domination of human-over-human.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1958, Murray Bookchin defined himself as an <a href="/wiki/Anarchist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anarchist">anarchist</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-youtube2007_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube2007-34">[34]</a></sup> seeing parallels between anarchism and ecology. His first book, <i><a href="/wiki/Our_Synthetic_Environment" title="Our Synthetic Environment">Our Synthetic Environment</a>,</i> was published under the <a href="/wiki/Pseudonym" title="Pseudonym">pseudonym</a> Lewis Herber in 1962, a few months before <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Carson" title="Rachel Carson">Rachel Carson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Silent_Spring" title="Silent Spring">Silent Spring</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> The book described a broad range of environmental ills but received little attention because of its political radicalism. His groundbreaking essay "Ecology and Revolutionary Thought" introduced <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a> as a concept in radical politics.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In 1968 he founded another group that published the influential <i>Anarchos</i> magazine, which published that and other innovative essays on post-scarcity and on ecological technologies such as solar and wind energy, and on decentralization and miniaturization. Lecturing throughout the United States, he helped popularize the concept of ecology to the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture" title="Counterculture">counterculture</a>.</p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Post-Scarcity_Anarchism" title="Post-Scarcity Anarchism">Post-Scarcity Anarchism</a></i> is a collection of <a href="/wiki/Essay" title="Essay">essays</a> written by <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a> and first published in 1971 by Ramparts Press.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> It outlines the possible form <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a> might take under conditions of <a href="/wiki/Post_scarcity" class="mw-redirect" title="Post scarcity">post-scarcity</a>. It is one of Bookchin's major works,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and its radical thesis provoked controversy for being <a href="/wiki/Utopia" title="Utopia">utopian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Messianism" title="Messianism">messianic</a> in its faith in the liberatory potential of <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-call_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-call-39">[39]</a></sup> Bookchin argues that <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial_society" title="Post-industrial society">post-industrial societies</a> are also post-scarcity societies, and can thus imagine "the fulfillment of the social and cultural potentialities latent in a technology of abundance".<sup id="cite_ref-call_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-call-39">[39]</a></sup> The self-administration of society is now made possible by technological advancement and, when technology is used in an ecologically sensitive manner, the revolutionary potential of society will be much changed.<sup id="cite_ref-AK_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AK-40">[40]</a></sup> In 1982, his book <i>The Ecology of Freedom</i> had a profound impact on the emerging ecology movement, both in the United States and abroad. He was a principal figure in the Burlington Greens in 1986-90, an ecology group that ran candidates for city council on a program to create neighborhood democracy.</p>
<p>Bookchin later developed a political philosophy to complement social ecology which he called "<a href="/wiki/Communalism_(Political_Philosophy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Communalism (Political Philosophy)">Communalism</a>" (spelled with a capital "C" to differentiate it from other forms of communalism). While originally conceived as a form of <a href="/wiki/Social_anarchism" title="Social anarchism">Social anarchism</a>, he later developed Communalism into a separate ideology which incorporates what he saw as the most beneficial elements of Anarchism, Marxism, syndicalism, and radical ecology.</p>
<p>Politically, Communalists advocate a network of directly democratic citizens' assemblies in individual communities/cities organized in a confederal fashion. This method used to achieve this is called <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Municipalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Libertarian Municipalism">Libertarian Municipalism</a> which involves the establishment of face-to-face democratic institutions which are to grow and expand confederally with the goal of eventually replacing the nation-state.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s.E2.80.931990s_.E2.80.93_Rise_of_environmentalism_and_engagement_with_Marxism_and_.27actually_existing_socialism.27">1970s–1990s – Rise of environmentalism and engagement with Marxism and 'actually existing socialism'</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1970s–1990s – Rise of environmentalism and engagement with Marxism and 'actually existing socialism'">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Barry_Commoner" title="Barry Commoner">Barry Commoner</a>, suggesting a <a href="/wiki/Left-wing" class="mw-redirect" title="Left-wing">left-wing</a> response to the <i><a href="/wiki/Limits_to_Growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Limits to Growth">Limits to Growth</a></i> model that predicted catastrophic <a href="/wiki/Resource_depletion" title="Resource depletion">resource depletion</a> and spurred <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>, postulated that capitalist technologies were chiefly responsible for <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a>, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Human_overpopulation" title="Human overpopulation">population pressures</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Commoner_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commoner-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East German</a> dissident writer and activist <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Bahro" title="Rudolf Bahro">Rudolf Bahro</a> published two books addressing the relationship between socialism and ecology – <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Alternative_in_Eastern_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Alternative in Eastern Europe (page does not exist)">The Alternative in Eastern Europe</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Bahro_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bahro-42">[42]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Socialism_and_Survival&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Socialism and Survival (page does not exist)">Socialism and Survival</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Bahro1_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bahro1-43">[43]</a></sup> – which promoted a 'new party' and led to his arrest, for which he gained international notoriety.</p>
<p>At around the same time, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alan_Roberts_(activist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alan Roberts (activist) (page does not exist)">Alan Roberts</a>, an Australian <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxist</a>, posited that people's unfulfilled needs fuelled <a href="/wiki/Consumerism" title="Consumerism">consumerism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-44">[44]</a></sup> Fellow Australian <a href="/wiki/Ted_Trainer" title="Ted Trainer">Ted Trainer</a> further called upon <a href="/wiki/Socialists" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialists">socialists</a> to develop a system that met human needs, in contrast to the capitalist system of created wants.<sup id="cite_ref-Trainer_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trainer-45">[45]</a></sup> A key development in the 1980s was the creation of the journal <i><a href="/wiki/Capitalism,_Nature,_Socialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitalism, Nature, Socialism">Capitalism, Nature, Socialism</a></i> (CNS) with <a href="/wiki/James_O%27Connor_(academic)" title="James O'Connor (academic)">James O'Connor</a> as founding editor and the first issue in 1988. The debates ensued led to a host of theoretical works by O'Connor, <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Merchant" title="Carolyn Merchant">Carolyn Merchant</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paul_Burkett&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paul Burkett (page does not exist)">Paul Burkett</a> and others.</p>
<p>The Australian <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Socialist_Perspective" title="Democratic Socialist Perspective">Democratic Socialist Party</a> launched the <a href="/wiki/Green_Left_Weekly" title="Green Left Weekly">Green Left Weekly</a> newspaper in 1991, following a period of working within Green Alliance and Green Party groups in formation. This ceased when the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Greens" title="Australian Greens">Australian Greens</a> adopted a policy of proscription of other political groups in August 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The DSP also published a comprehensive policy resolution, "Socialism and Human Survival" in book form in 1990, with an expanded second edition in 1999 entitled "Environment, Capitalism &amp; Socialism".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s_onwards_-_Engagement_with_the_anti-globalization_movement_and_The_Ecosocialist_Manifesto">1990s onwards - Engagement with the anti-globalization movement and The Ecosocialist Manifesto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1990s onwards - Engagement with the anti-globalization movement and The Ecosocialist Manifesto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1990s saw the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_feminism" title="Socialist feminism">socialist feminists</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mary_Mellor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mary Mellor (page does not exist)">Mary Mellor</a><sup id="cite_ref-Mellor_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mellor-48">[48]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Salleh" title="Ariel Salleh">Ariel Salleh</a><sup id="cite_ref-Salleh_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Salleh-49">[49]</a></sup> address environmental issues within an eco-socialist paradigm. With the rising profile of the <a href="/wiki/Anti-globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-globalization">anti-globalization</a> movement in the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>, an "<a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> of the poor", combining <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> awareness and <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>, has also become prominent.<sup id="cite_ref-Guha_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guha-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Pepper_(Eco-socialist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="David Pepper (Eco-socialist) (page does not exist)">David Pepper</a> also released his important work, <i>Ecosocialism: From Deep Ecology to Social Justice</i>, in 1994, which critiques the current approach of many within Green politics, particularly <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecologists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DPepper_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DPepper-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2001, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Joel Kovel</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social scientist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">psychiatrist</a> and former candidate for the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Party (United States)">Green Party of the United States</a> (GPUS) <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">Presidential</a> nomination in 2000, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_L%C3%B6wy" title="Michael Löwy">Michael Löwy</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropologist</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/Reunified_Fourth_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Reunified Fourth International">Reunified Fourth International</a> (a principal <a href="/wiki/Trotskyist" class="mw-redirect" title="Trotskyist">Trotskyist</a> organisation), released <i>An ecosocialist manifesto</i>, which has been adopted by some organisations<sup id="cite_ref-GLSite_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GLSite-21">[21]</a></sup> and suggests possible routes for the growth of eco-socialist consciousness.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kovel's 2002 work, <i>The Enemy of Nature: The End of Capitalism or the End of the World?</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup> is considered by many to be the most up-to-date exposition of eco-socialist thought.<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2007, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Ecosocialist_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Ecosocialist Network (page does not exist)">International Ecosocialist Network</a> was founded in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_on_current_Green_and_socialist_movements">Influence on current Green and socialist movements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Influence on current Green and socialist movements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Currently, many <a href="/wiki/Green_Parties" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Parties">Green Parties</a> around the world, such as the <a href="/wiki/GreenLeft" class="mw-redirect" title="GreenLeft">Dutch Green Left Party</a> (GroenLinks)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> , contain strong eco-socialist elements. Radical <a href="/wiki/Red-green_alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Red-green alliance">Red-green alliances</a> have been formed in many countries by eco-socialists, radical <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Greens</a> and other radical left groups. In Denmark, the <a href="/wiki/Red-Green_Alliance_(Denmark)" title="Red-Green Alliance (Denmark)">Red-Green Alliance</a> was formed as a coalition of numerous radical parties. Within the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, a number of <a href="/wiki/Far-left" class="mw-redirect" title="Far-left">far-left</a> parties from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern Europe</a> have organized themselves into the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Green_Left_Alliance" title="Nordic Green Left Alliance">Nordic Green Left Alliance</a>. Red Greens feature heavily in the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Saskatchewan" title="Green Party of Saskatchewan">Green Party of Saskatchewan</a> (in Canada but not necessarily affiliated to the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Canada" title="Green Party of Canada">Green Party of Canada</a>) and then-recently <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Party (United States)">GPUS</a> that officially adopted ideology within party.<sup id="cite_ref-gp.org_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gp.org-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party of England and Wales</a> features an eco-socialist group, <a href="/wiki/Green_Left_(UK)" title="Green Left (UK)">Green Left</a>, that was founded in June 2005 and whose members hold a number of influential positions within the party, including both the former <a href="/wiki/Principal_Speaker" title="Principal Speaker">Principal Speakers</a> <a href="/wiki/Si%C3%A2n_Berry" title="Siân Berry">Siân Berry</a> and Dr. <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Derek Wall</a>, himself an eco-socialist and Marxist academic, as well as prominent <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_England_and_Wales" title="Green Party of England and Wales">Green Party</a> candidate and human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tatchell" title="Peter Tatchell">Peter Tatchell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GLSite_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GLSite-21">[21]</a></sup> Many Marxist organisations also contain eco-socialists, as evidenced by <a href="/wiki/Michael_L%C3%B6wy" title="Michael Löwy">Löwy's</a> involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Reunified_Fourth_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Reunified Fourth International">reunified Fourth International</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Socialist_Resistance" title="Socialist Resistance">Socialist Resistance</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Marxist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> newspaper that reports on eco-socialist issues and has published two collections of essays on eco-socialist thought: <i>Ecosocialism or Barbarism?</i>, edited by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jane_Kelly_(eco-socialist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jane Kelly (eco-socialist) (page does not exist)">Jane Kelly</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheila_Malone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sheila Malone (page does not exist)">Sheila Malone</a>, and <i>The Global Fight for Climate Justice</i>, edited by <a href="/wiki/Ian_Angus_(activist)" title="Ian Angus (activist)">Ian Angus</a> with a foreword by Derek Wall.<sup id="cite_ref-SR_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SR-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SRBooks_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SRBooks-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_on_.22existing_socialist.22_regimes">Influence on "existing socialist" regimes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Influence on &quot;existing socialist&quot; regimes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eco-socialism has had a minor influence over developments in the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy" title="Environmental policy">environmental policies</a> of what can be called "existing <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a>" regimes, notably the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">People's Republic of China</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pan_Yue" title="Pan Yue">Pan Yue</a>, Deputy Director of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">PRC</a>'s <a href="/wiki/State_Environmental_Protection_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="State Environmental Protection Administration">State Environmental Protection Administration</a>, has acknowledged the influence of eco-socialist theory on his championing of <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> within <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">China</a>, which has gained him international acclaim (including being nominated for the Person of the Year Award 2006 by <i><a href="/wiki/New_Statesman" title="New Statesman">The New Statesman</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-NSYue_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSYue-55">[55]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> current affairs magazine). <a href="/wiki/Pan_Yue" title="Pan Yue">Yue</a> stated in an interview that, while he often finds eco-socialist theory "too idealistic" and lacking "ways of solving actual problems", he believes that it provides "political reference for China’s scientific view of development", "gives socialist ideology room to expand" and offers "a theoretical basis for the establishment of fair international rules" on the <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environment</a>.</p>
<p>He echoes much of eco-socialist thought, attacking international "environmental inequality", refusing to focus on <a href="/wiki/Technological_fix" title="Technological fix">technological fixes</a> and arguing for the construction of "a harmonious, resource-saving and environmentally-friendly society". He also shows a knowledge of eco-socialist history, from the convergence of radical green politics and socialism and their political "<a href="/wiki/Red-green_alliance" class="mw-redirect" title="Red-green alliance">red-green alliances</a>" in the post-<a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> era. This focus on eco-socialism has informed an essay, <i>On Socialist Ecological Civilisation</i>, published in September 2006, which, according to <a href="/wiki/Chinadialogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinadialogue">chinadialogue</a>, "sparked debate" in <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-YueInterview_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YueInterview-56">[56]</a></sup> The current <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bolivia" title="Constitution of Bolivia">Constitution of Bolivia</a>, promulgated in 2009, is the first both ecologic and pro-socialist Constitution in the world, making the Bolivian state officially ecosocialist.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecosocialist_International_Network_.28EIN.29_and_other_international_eco-socialist_organisations">Ecosocialist International Network (EIN) and other international eco-socialist organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ecosocialist International Network (EIN) and other international eco-socialist organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007, it was announced that attempts to form an <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ecosocialist_International_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ecosocialist International Network (page does not exist)">Ecosocialist International Network</a> (EIN) would be made and an inaugural meeting of the International occurred on October 7, 2007 in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-InternationalAnnounce_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-InternationalAnnounce-58">[58]</a></sup> The meeting attracted "more than 60 activists from Argentina, Australia, Belgium, Brazil, Canada, Cyprus, Denmark, France, Greece, Italy, Switzerland, United Kingdom, and the United States" and elected a Steering Committee featuring representatives from Britain, the United States, Canada, France, Greece, Argentina, Brazil and Australia, including <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Joel Kovel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_L%C3%B6wy" title="Michael Löwy">Michael Löwy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Derek Wall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Angus_(activist)" title="Ian Angus (activist)">Ian Angus</a> (editor of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.climateandcapitalism.com">Climate and Capitalism</a> in Canada) and <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Salleh" title="Ariel Salleh">Ariel Salleh</a>. The Committee states that it wants "to incorporate members from China, India, Africa, Oceania and Eastern Europe". EIN held its second international conference in January 2009, in association with the next <a href="/wiki/World_Social_Forum" title="World Social Forum">World Social Forum</a> in Brazil".<sup id="cite_ref-International_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-International-59">[59]</a></sup> The conference released The Belem Ecosocialist Declaration.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>International networking by eco-socialists has already been seen in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Praxis_Research_and_Education_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Praxis Research and Education Center (page does not exist)">Praxis Research and Education Center</a>, a group on international researchers and activists. Based in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> and established in 1997, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Praxis_Research_and_Education_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Praxis Research and Education Center (page does not exist)">Praxis</a>, as well as publishing books "by <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_socialism" title="Libertarian socialism">libertarian socialists</a>, Marxist <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchists</a>, [and] <a href="/wiki/Syndicalism" title="Syndicalism">syndicalists</a>", running the <a href="/wiki/Victor_Serge" title="Victor Serge">Victor Serge</a> Library and opposing <a href="/wiki/Second_Chechen_War" title="Second Chechen War">war in Chechnya</a>, states that it believes "that capitalism has brought life on the planet near to the brink of catastrophe, and that a form of ecosocialism needs to emerge to replace capitalism before it is too late".<sup id="cite_ref-PraxisUSSF_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PraxisUSSF-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PraxisRU_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PraxisRU-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_capitalist_expansion_and_globalisation">Critique of capitalist expansion and globalisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Critique of capitalist expansion and globalisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Merging aspects of <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a>, socialism, <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> and ecology, eco-socialists generally believe that the <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> system is the cause of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">inequality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a> through <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> and imperialism under the supervision of repressive states and transnational structures.</p>
<p>In the <i>Ecosocialist manifesto</i>, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_L%C3%B6wy" title="Michael Löwy">Löwy</a> suggest that capitalist expansion causes both "crises of ecology" through "rampant <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>" and "societal breakdown" that springs "from the form of imperialism known as globalization". They believe that capitalism's expansion "exposes <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>" to <a href="/wiki/Pollutants" class="mw-redirect" title="Pollutants">pollutants</a>, habitat destruction and <a href="/wiki/Resource_depletion" title="Resource depletion">resource depletion</a>, "reducing the sensuous vitality of <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a> to the cold exchangeability required for the accumulation of <a href="/wiki/Capital_(economics)" title="Capital (economics)">capital</a>", while submerging "the majority of the world's people to a mere reservoir of <a href="/wiki/Labour_(economics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Labour (economics)">labor</a> power" as it penetrates communities through "<a href="/wiki/Consumerism" title="Consumerism">consumerism</a> and depoliticization".<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Other eco-socialists, like <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a>, highlight how, in the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free-market" class="mw-redirect" title="Free-market">free-market</a> capitalism structures economies to produce <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">export-geared crops</a> that take water from traditional <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_farming" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence farming">subsistence farms</a>, increasing hunger and the likelihood of <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a>; furthermore, forests are increasingly <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">cleared</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enclosure" title="Enclosure">enclosed</a> to produce <a href="/wiki/Cash_crops" class="mw-redirect" title="Cash crops">cash crops</a> that separate people from their local <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> and aggravate <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>. <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a> shows that many of the world's poor have access to the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> through "non-monetised communal <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>", such as <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_farming" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence farming">subsistence farming</a>, but, despite providing for need and a level of prosperity, these are not included in conventional economics measures, like <a href="/wiki/Measures_of_national_income_and_output" title="Measures of national income and output">GNP</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a> therefore views <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neo-liberal</a> globalization as "part of the long struggle of the state and commercial interests to steal from those who subsist" by removing "access to the resources that sustain ordinary people across the globe".<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup> Furthermore, Kovel sees <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">neoliberalism</a> as "a return to the pure logic of capital" that "has effectively swept away measures which had inhibited capital’s aggressivity, replacing them with naked exploitation of humanity and nature"; for Kovel, this "tearing down of boundaries and limits to accumulation is known as globalization", which was "a deliberate response to a serious accumulation crisis (in the 1970s) that had convinced the leaders of the global economy to install what we know as neoliberalism.".<sup id="cite_ref-KovelNSG_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KovelNSG-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Ramachandra_Guha" title="Ramachandra Guha">Guha</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Martinez-Alier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Juan Martinez-Alier (page does not exist)">Martinez-Alier</a> blame globalization for creating increased levels of <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">waste</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>, and then dumping the <a href="/wiki/Waste" title="Waste">waste</a> on the most vulnerable in society, particularly those in the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guha_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guha-12">[12]</a></sup> Others have also noted that capitalism disproportionately affects the poorest in the <a href="/wiki/Global_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Global North">Global North</a> as well, leading to examples of resistance such as the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_justice" title="Environmental justice">environmental justice</a> movement in the United States, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> people and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic minorities">ethnic minorities</a> who highlight the tendency for waste dumps, major road projects and <a href="/wiki/Incinerator" class="mw-redirect" title="Incinerator">incinerators</a> to be constructed around socially excluded areas. However, as <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a> highlights, such campaigns are often ignored or persecuted precisely because they originate among the most marginalized in society: the <a href="/wiki/African-American" class="mw-redirect" title="African-American">African-American</a> radical green religious group <a href="/wiki/MOVE" title="MOVE">MOVE</a>, campaigning for ecological revolution and <a href="/wiki/Animal_rights" title="Animal rights">animal rights</a> from <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, had many members imprisoned or even killed by US authorities from the 1970s onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eco-socialism disagrees with the elite theories of capitalism, which tend to label a specific <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">class</a> or social group as conspirators who construct a system that satisfies their greed and personal desires. Instead, eco-socialists suggest that the very system itself is self-perpetuating, fuelled by "extra-human" or "impersonal" forces. Kovel uses the <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_disaster" title="Bhopal disaster">Bhopal industrial disaster</a> as an example. Many <a href="/wiki/Anti-corporate_activism" title="Anti-corporate activism">anti-corporate</a> observers would blame the avarice of those at the top of many <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multi-national corporations</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Union_Carbide" title="Union Carbide">Union Carbide</a> Corporation in <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_disaster" title="Bhopal disaster">Bhopal</a>, for seemingly isolated <a href="/wiki/Industrial_accident" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial accident">industrial accidents</a>. Conversely, Kovel suggests that <a href="/wiki/Bhopal_disaster" title="Bhopal disaster">Union Carbide</a> were experiencing a decrease in sales that led to falling profits, which, due to <a href="/wiki/Stock_market" title="Stock market">stock market</a> conditions, translated into a drop in share values. The depreciation of share value made many <a href="/wiki/Shareholders" class="mw-redirect" title="Shareholders">shareholders</a> sell their stock, weakening the company and leading to cost-cutting measures that eroded the safety procedures and mechanisms at the Bhopal site. Though this did not, in Kovel's mind, make the Bhopal disaster inevitable, he believes that it illustrates the effect <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a> forces can have on increasing the likelihood of ecological and social problems.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_and_exchange_value">Use and exchange value</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Use and exchange value">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eco-socialism focuses closely on <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marx's</a> theories about the contradiction between <a href="/wiki/Use_value" title="Use value">use values</a> and <a href="/wiki/Exchange_value" title="Exchange value">exchange values</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> posits that, within a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, goods are not produced to meet needs but are produced to be exchanged for money that we then use to acquire other goods; as we have to keep selling in order to keep buying, we must persuade others to buy our goods just to ensure our survival, which leads to the production of goods with no previous use that can be sold to sustain our ability to buy other goods.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Such goods, in an eco-socialist analysis, produce <a href="/wiki/Exchange_value" title="Exchange value">exchange values</a> but have no <a href="/wiki/Use_value" title="Use value">use value</a>. Eco-socialists like Kovel stress that this contradiction has reached a destructive extent, where certain essential activities - such as caring for relatives full-time and basic <a href="/wiki/Subsistence" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsistence">subsistence</a> – are unrewarded, while unnecessary commodities earn individuals huge fortunes and fuel <a href="/wiki/Consumerism" title="Consumerism">consumerism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Resource_depletion" title="Resource depletion">resource depletion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22second_contradiction.22_of_capitalism">The "second contradiction" of capitalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The &quot;second contradiction&quot; of capitalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/James_O%27Connor_(academic)" title="James O'Connor (academic)">James O'Connor</a> argues for a "second contradiction" of underproduction, to complement <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marx</a>'s "first" contradiction of capital and labor. While the second contradiction is often considered a theory of environmental degradation, O'Connor's theory in fact goes much further. Building on the work of Karl Polanyi, along with Marx, O'Connor argues that capitalism necessarily undermines the "conditions of production" necessary to sustain the endless accumulation of capital. These conditions of production include soil, water, energy, and so forth. But they also include an adequate public education system, transportation infrastructures, and other services that are not produced directly by capital, but which capital needs in order accumulate effectively. As the conditions of production are exhausted, the costs of production for capital increase. For this reason, the second contradiction generates an underproduction crisis tendency, with the rising cost of inputs and labor, to complement the overproduction tendency of too many commodities for too few customers. Like Marx's contradiction of capital and labor, the second contradiction therefore threatens the system's existence.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, O'Connor believes that, in order to remedy environmental contradictions, the capitalist system innovates new technologies that overcome existing problems but introduce new ones.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>O'Connor cites <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> as an example, which he sees as a form of producing energy that is advertised as an alternative to carbon-intensive, non-renewable <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">fossil fuels</a>, but creates long-term <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_waste" title="Radioactive waste">radioactive waste</a> and other dangers to health and security. While O'Connor believes that capitalism is capable of spreading out its economic supports so widely that it can afford to destroy one <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a> before moving onto another, he and many other eco-socialists now fear that, with the onset of globalization, the system is running out of new <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor-64">[64]</a></sup> Kovel adds that capitalist firms have to continue to extract profit through a combination of intensive or extensive exploitation and selling to new markets, meaning that capitalism must <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">grow</a> indefinitely to exist, which he thinks is impossible on a planet of finite resources.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_role_of_the_state_and_transnational_organisations">The role of the state and transnational organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The role of the state and transnational organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">Capitalist</a> expansion is seen by eco-socialists as being "hand in glove" with "corrupt and subservient client states" that repress dissent against the system, governed by <a href="/wiki/International_organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="International organisation">international organisations</a> "under the overall supervision of the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western powers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> United States", which subordinate peripheral nations economically and militarily.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> further claims that capitalism itself spurs conflict and, ultimately, <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a>. Kovel states that the '<a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>', between <a href="/wiki/Islamist_extremists" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamist extremists">Islamist extremists</a> and the United States, is caused by "oil imperialism", whereby the capitalist nations require control over sources of <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a>, especially oil, which are necessary to continue intensive <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">industrial growth</a> - in the quest for control of such resources, Kovel argues that the capitalist nations, specifically the United States, have come into conflict with the predominantly <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> nations where oil is often found.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Eco-socialists believe that state or self-<a href="/wiki/Regulatory_economics" title="Regulatory economics">regulation</a> of markets does not solve the crisis "because to do so requires setting limits upon accumulation", which is "unacceptable" for a <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growth</a>-orientated system; they believe that <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a> and revolutionary impulses cannot be tackled properly "because to do so would mean abandoning the logic of <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">empire</a>". Instead, eco-socialists feel that increasing repressive <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a> increases <a href="/wiki/Social_alienation" title="Social alienation">alienation</a> and causes further <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a> and believe that state <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorist</a> methods are, in Kovel and <a href="/wiki/Michael_L%C3%B6wy" title="Michael Löwy">Löwy</a>'s words, "evolving into a new and malignant variation of <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a>". They echo <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg" title="Rosa Luxemburg">Rosa Luxemburg</a>'s "stark choice" between "socialism or barbarism", which was believed to be a prediction of the coming of <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a> and further forms of destructive capitalism at the beginning of the twentieth century (<a href="/wiki/Rosa_Luxemburg" title="Rosa Luxemburg">Luxemburg</a> was in fact murdered by proto-<a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">Freikorps</a> in the revolutionary atmosphere of Germany in 1919).<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tensions_within_the_Eco-Socialist_discourse">Tensions within the Eco-Socialist discourse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tensions within the Eco-Socialist discourse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Reflecting tensions within the environmental and socialist movements, there is some conflict of ideas. In practice however, a synthesis is emerging which calls for democratic regulation of industry in the interests of people and the environment, nationalisation of some key (environmental) industries, local democracy and an extension of co-ops and the library principle.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_other_forms_of_green_politics">Critique of other forms of green politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Critique of other forms of green politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a single <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">source</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Eco-socialism#.23" title="Talk:Eco-socialism">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <small><i>(May 2013)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Eco-socialists criticise many within the <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green movement</a> for not being overtly <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a>, for working within the existing <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statism" title="Statism">statist</a> system, for <a href="/wiki/Voluntarism_(action)" title="Voluntarism (action)">voluntarism</a>, or for reliance on technological fixes. The eco-socialist ideology is based on a critique of other forms of Green politics, including various forms of <a href="/wiki/Green_economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Green economics">Green economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Localism_(politics)" title="Localism (politics)">Localism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_Ecology" class="mw-redirect" title="Deep Ecology">Deep Ecology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bioregionalism" title="Bioregionalism">Bioregionalism</a> and even some manifestations of radical <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">green ideologies</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Eco-feminism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-feminism">Eco-feminism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_Ecology" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Ecology">Social Ecology</a>.</p>
<p>As Kovel puts it, eco-socialism differs from Green politics at the most fundamental level because the '<a href="/w/index.php?title=Four_Pillars_of_the_Green_Party&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Four Pillars of the Green Party (page does not exist)">Four Pillars</a>' of Green politics (and the 'Ten Key Values' of the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Party (United States)">US Green Party</a>) do not include the demand for the <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_of_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Emancipation of labour">emancipation of labour</a> and the end of the separation between producers and the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many eco-socialists also oppose <a href="/wiki/Malthusianism" title="Malthusianism">Malthusianism</a><sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup> and are alarmed by the gulf between Green politics in the <a href="/wiki/Global_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Global North">Global North</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guha_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guha-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_within-system_approaches.2C_voluntarism_and_technological_fixes">Opposition to within-system approaches, voluntarism and technological fixes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Opposition to within-system approaches, voluntarism and technological fixes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eco-socialists are highly critical of those <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Greens</a> who favour "working within the system". While eco-socialists like <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> recognise the ability of within-system approaches to raise awareness, and believe that "the struggle for an <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecologically</a> rational world must include a struggle for the state", he believes that the mainstream Green movement is too easily co-opted by the current powerful socio-political forces as it "passes from citizen-based <a href="/wiki/Activism" title="Activism">activism</a> to ponderous bureaucracies scuffling for 'a seat at the table'".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>For Kovel, capitalism is "happy to enlist" the Green movement for "convenience", "control over popular dissent" and "rationalization". He further attacks within-system green initiatives like <a href="/wiki/Carbon_emission_trading" title="Carbon emission trading">carbon trading</a>, which he sees as a "capitalist shell game" that turns <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> "into a fresh source of profit".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears.
