(June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_Tokar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brian Tokar (page does not exist)">Brian Tokar</a> has further criticised carbon trading in this way, suggesting that it augments existing class inequality and gives the "largest 'players'... substantial control over the whole 'game'".<sup id="cite_ref-Tokar_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tokar-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition, Kovel criticises the "defeatism" of <a href="/wiki/Voluntarism_(action)" title="Voluntarism (action)">voluntarism</a> in some local forms of <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> that do not connect: he suggests that they can be "drawn off into <a href="/wiki/Individualism" title="Individualism">individualism</a>" or co-opted to the demands of capitalism, as in the case of certain <a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recycling</a> projects, where citizens are "induced to provide free labor" to <a href="/wiki/Waste_management" title="Waste management">waste management</a> industries who are involved in the "capitalization of nature". He labels the notion on <a href="/wiki/Voluntarism_(action)" title="Voluntarism (action)">voluntarism</a> "<a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">ecopolitics</a> without struggle".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Technological fixes to <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> problems are also rejected by eco-socialists. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saral_Sarkar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Saral Sarkar (page does not exist)">Saral Sarkar</a> has updated the thesis of 1970s '<a href="/wiki/Limits_to_growth" class="mw-redirect" title="Limits to growth">limits to growth</a>' to exemplify the limits of new capitalist technologies such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_fuel_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrogen fuel cell">hydrogen fuel cells</a>, which require large amounts of energy to split molecules to obtain hydrogen.<sup id="cite_ref-Sarkar_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sarkar-68">[68]</a></sup> Furthermore, Kovel notes that "events in nature are reciprocal and multi-determined" and can therefore not be predictably "fixed"; socially, technologies cannot solve social problems because they are not "mechanical". He posits an eco-socialist analysis, developed from <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marx</a>, that patterns of production and social organisation are more important than the forms of technology used within a given configuration of society.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, he suggests that technology "has been the <i>sine qua non</i> of <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growth</a>" - thus he believes that, even in a world with hypothetical "free energy", the effect would be to lower the cost of <a href="/wiki/Automobile" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile">automobile</a> production, leading to the massive <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">overproduction</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicles</a>, "collapsing infrastructure", chronic <a href="/wiki/Resource_depletion" title="Resource depletion">resource depletion</a> and the "paving over" of the "remainder of <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a>". In the modern world, Kovel considers the supposed efficiency of new <a href="/wiki/Post-industrial" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-industrial">post-industrial</a> commodities is a "plain illusion", as <a href="/wiki/Miniaturization" title="Miniaturization">miniaturized</a> components involve many substances and are therefore non-<a href="/wiki/Recycling" title="Recycling">recyclable</a> (and, theoretically, only simple substances could be retrieved by burning out-of-date equipment, releasing more <a href="/wiki/Pollutants" class="mw-redirect" title="Pollutants">pollutants</a>). He is quick to warn "environmental <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberals</a>" against over-selling the virtues of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energies</a> that cannot meet the mass energy consumption of the era; although he would still support <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> projects, he believes it is more important to restructure societies to reduce energy use before relying on <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> technologies alone.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_Green_economics">Critique of Green economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Critique of Green economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eco-socialists have based their ideas for political strategy on a critique of several different trends in <a href="/wiki/Green_economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Green economics">Green economics</a>. At the most fundamental level, eco-socialists reject what Kovel calls "<a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics" title="Ecological economics">ecological economics</a>" or the "ecological wing of mainstream economics" for being "uninterested in social transformation". He furthers rejects the <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Neo-Smithian</a> school, who believe in <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a>'s vision of "a capitalism of small producers, freely exchanging with each other", which is self-regulating and competitive.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The school is represented by thinkers like <a href="/wiki/David_Korten" title="David Korten">David Korten</a> who believe in "regulated markets" checked by <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> and <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civil society</a> but, for Kovel, they do not provide a critique of the expansive nature of capitalism away from localised production and ignore "questions of <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">class</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a> or any other category of domination". Kovel also criticises their "fairy-tale" view of history, which refers to the abuse of "<a href="/wiki/Natural_capital" title="Natural capital">natural capital</a>" by the <a href="/wiki/Materialism" title="Materialism">materialism</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific Revolution">Scientific Revolution</a>, an assumption that, in Kovel's eyes, seems to suggest that "nature had toiled to put the gift of capital into human hands", rather than capitalism being a product of social relations in human history.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Other forms of <a href="/wiki/Community-based_economics" title="Community-based economics">Community-based economics</a> are also rejected by eco-socialists such as Kovel, including followers of <a href="/wiki/E._F._Schumacher" title="E. F. Schumacher">E. F. Schumacher</a> and some members of the <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperative movement">Cooperative movement</a>, for advocating "no more than a very halting and isolated first step". He thinks that their principles are "only partially realizable within the institutions of <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperative movement">cooperatives</a> in capitalist society" because "the internal cooperation" of <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperative movement">cooperatives</a> is "forever hemmed in and compromised" by the need to expand value and compete within the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marx</a> also believed that <a href="/wiki/Cooperative" title="Cooperative">cooperatives</a> within capitalism make workers into "their own capitalist... by enabling them to use the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> for the employment of their own labour".<sup id="cite_ref-Capital3_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capital3-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>For Kovel and other eco-socialists, <a href="/wiki/Community-based_economics" title="Community-based economics">Community-based economics</a> and Green <a href="/wiki/Localism_(politics)" title="Localism (politics)">Localism</a> are "a fantasy" because "strict <a href="/wiki/Localism_(politics)" title="Localism (politics)">localism</a> belongs to the aboriginal stages of society" and would be an "ecological nightmare at present population levels" due to "heat losses from a multitude of dispersed sites, the squandering of scarce resources, the needless reproduction of effort, and cultural impoverishment". While he feels that small-scale production units are "an essential part of the path towards an ecological society", he sees them not as "an end in itself"; in his view, small enterprises can be either capitalist or <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> in their configuration and therefore must be "consistently <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a>", through recognition and support of the emancipation of labour, and exist "in a dialectic with the whole of things", as human society will need large-scale projects, such as transport infrastructures.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>He highlights the work of <a href="/wiki/Steady-state_economy#Herman_Daly.27s_concept_of_a_steady-state_economy" title="Steady-state economy">steady-state theorist</a> <a href="/wiki/Herman_Daly" title="Herman Daly">Herman Daly</a>, who exemplifies what eco-socialists see as the good and bad points of <a href="/wiki/Ecological_economics" title="Ecological economics">ecological economics</a> — while Daly offers a critique of capitalism and a desire for "workers ownership", he only believes in workers ownership "kept firmly within a capitalist market", ignoring the eco-socialist desire for struggle in the emancipation of labour and hoping that the interests of labour and management today can be improved so that they are "in harmony".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_Deep_Ecology">Critique of Deep Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Critique of Deep Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite the inclusion of both in political factions like the '<a href="/wiki/Fundies" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundies">Fundies</a>' of the <a href="/wiki/German_Green_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="German Green Party">German Green Party</a>, eco-socialists and <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecologists</a> hold markedly opposite views. Eco-socialists like Kovel have attacked <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecology</a> because, like other forms of Green politics and <a href="/wiki/Green_economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Green economics">Green economics</a>, it features "virtuous souls" who have "no internal connection with the critique of capitalism and the emancipation of labor". Kovel is particularly scathing about <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecology</a> and its "fatuous pronouncement" that Green politics is "neither left nor right, but ahead", which, for him, ignores the notion that "that which does not confront the system comes its instrument".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Even more scathingly, Kovel suggests that in "its effort to decentre humanity within nature", <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecologists</a> can "go too far" and argue for the "splitting away of unwanted people", as evidenced by their desire to preserve <a href="/wiki/Wilderness" title="Wilderness">wilderness</a> by removing the groups that have lived there "from <a href="/wiki/Time_immemorial" title="Time immemorial">time immemorial</a>". Kovel thinks that this lends legitimacy to "<a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> elites", like the <a href="/wiki/US_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, who can make preservation of <a href="/wiki/Wilderness" title="Wilderness">wilderness</a> a part of their projects that "have added value as sites for <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a>" but remove people from their land. Between 1986 and 1996, Kovel notes that over three million people were displaced by "conservation projects"; in the making of the <a href="/wiki/US_National_Parks" class="mw-redirect" title="US National Parks">US National Parks</a>, three hundred <a href="/wiki/Shoshone" title="Shoshone">Shoshone</a> <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Indians</a> were killed in the development of <a href="/wiki/Yosemite" class="mw-redirect" title="Yosemite">Yosemite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kovel believes that <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecology</a> has affected the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green movement</a> and led to calls from restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>, "often allying with reactionaries in a... cryptically <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racist</a> quest".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Indeed, he finds traces of <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecology</a> in the "biological reduction" of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a>, an ideology many "organicist thinkers" have found appealing, including <a href="/w/index.php?title=Herbert_Gruhl&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Herbert Gruhl (page does not exist)">Herbert Gruhl</a>, a founder of the <a href="/wiki/German_Green_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="German Green Party">German Green Party</a> (who subsequently left when it became more <a href="/wiki/Left-wing" class="mw-redirect" title="Left-wing">Left-wing</a>) and originator of the phrase "neither left nor right, but ahead". Kovel warns that, while '<a href="/wiki/Ecofascism" title="Ecofascism">ecofascism</a>' is confined to a narrow band of <a href="/wiki/Far_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Far right">far right</a> intellectuals and disaffected <a href="/wiki/White_power_skinhead" title="White power skinhead">white power skinheads</a> who involved themselves alongside <a href="/wiki/Far_left" class="mw-redirect" title="Far left">far left</a> groups in the <a href="/wiki/Anti-globalization_movement" title="Anti-globalization movement">anti-globalization movement</a>, it may be "imposed as a <a href="/wiki/Revolution_from_above" title="Revolution from above">revolution from above</a> to install an <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a> regime in order to preserve the main workings of the system" in times of crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_bioregionalism">Critique of bioregionalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Critique of bioregionalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bioregionalism" title="Bioregionalism">Bioregionalism</a>, a philosophy developed by writers like <a href="/wiki/Kirkpatrick_Sale" title="Kirkpatrick Sale">Kirkpatrick Sale</a> who believe in the self-sufficiency of "appropriate bioregional boundaries" drawn up by inhabitants of "an area",<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> has been thoroughly critiqued by <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a>, who fears that the "vagueness" of the area will lead to conflict and further boundaries between communities.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While <a href="/wiki/Kirkpatrick_Sale" title="Kirkpatrick Sale">Sale</a> cites the <a href="/wiki/Bioregionalism" title="Bioregionalism">bioregional</a> living of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kovel notes that such ideas are impossible to translate to populations of modern proportions, and evidences the fact that <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> held land in <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a>, rather than <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a> - thus, for eco-socialists, <a href="/wiki/Bioregionalism" title="Bioregionalism">bioregionalism</a> provides no understanding of what is needed to transform society, and what the inevitable "response of the capitalist state" would be to people constructing <a href="/wiki/Bioregionalism" title="Bioregionalism">bioregionalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kovel also attacks the problems of self-sufficiency. Where <a href="/wiki/Kirkpatrick_Sale" title="Kirkpatrick Sale">Sale</a> believes in self-sufficient regions "each developing the energy of its peculiar ecology", such as "wood in the northwest [USA]",<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kovel asks "how on earth" these can be made sufficient for regional needs, and notes the environmental damage of converting <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> into a "forest-destroying and smoke-spewing wood-burning" city. Kovel also questions <a href="/wiki/Kirkpatrick_Sale" title="Kirkpatrick Sale">Sale</a>'s insistence on <a href="/wiki/Bioregionalism" title="Bioregionalism">bioregions</a> that do "not require connections with the outside, but within strict limits", and whether this precludes journeys to visit family members and other forms of travel.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_variants_of_eco-feminism">Critique of variants of eco-feminism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Critique of variants of eco-feminism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like many variants of socialism and Green politics, eco-socialists recognise the importance of "the gendered bifurcation of nature" and support the emancipation of <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a> as it "is at the root of <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">class</a>". Nevertheless, while Kovel believes that "any path out of capitalism must also be <a href="/wiki/Eco-feminism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-feminism">eco-feminist</a>", he criticises types of <a href="/wiki/Eco-feminism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-feminism">ecofeminism</a> that are not <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a> and can "essentialize women's closeness to nature and build from there, submerging history into nature", becoming more at place in the "comforts of the <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> Growth Centre". These limitations, for Kovel, "keep <a href="/wiki/Eco-feminism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-feminism">ecofeminism</a> from becoming a coherent social movement".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_Social_Ecology">Critique of Social Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Critique of Social Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While having much in common with the radical tradition of <a href="/wiki/Social_Ecology" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Ecology">Social Ecology</a>, eco-socialists still see themselves as distinct. <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> believes this is because Social Ecologists see hierarchy "in-itself" as the cause of <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> destruction, whereas eco-socialists focus on <a href="/wiki/Gender" title="Gender">gender</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">class</a> domination embodied in capitalism and recognise that forms of authority that are not "an expropriation of human power for... self-aggrandizement", such as a student-teacher relationship that is "reciprocal and mutual", are beneficial.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In practice, Kovel describes <a href="/wiki/Social_Ecology" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Ecology">Social Ecology</a> as continuing the <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchist</a> tradition of <a href="/wiki/Non-violent_direct_action" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violent direct action">non-violent direct action</a>, which is "necessary" but "not sufficient" because "it leaves unspoken the question of building an ecological society beyond <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capital</a>". Furthermore, Social Ecologists and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchists</a> tend to focus on the state alone, rather than the class relations behind state domination (in the view of <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marxists</a>). Kovel fears that this is political, springing from historic hostility to <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> among anarchists and sectarianism, which he points out as a fault of the "brilliant" but "dogmatic" founder of Social Ecology, <a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition_to_Malthusianism_and_Neo-Malthusianism">Opposition to Malthusianism and Neo-Malthusianism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Opposition to Malthusianism and Neo-Malthusianism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While <a href="/wiki/Malthusianism" title="Malthusianism">Malthusianism</a> and eco-socialism overlap within the <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green movement</a> because both address <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">over-industrialism</a>, and despite the fact that Eco-socialists, like many within the Green movement, are described as <a href="/wiki/Neo-malthusianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-malthusianism">neo-Malthusian</a> because of their criticism of <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>, Eco-socialists are opposed to <a href="/wiki/Malthusianism" title="Malthusianism">Malthusianism</a>. This divergence stems from the difference between <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Marxist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malthusianism" title="Malthusianism">Malthusian</a> examinations of social injustice - whereas Marx blames <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a> on <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">class</a> injustice, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Malthus" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Malthus">Malthus</a> argued that the <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> remained poor because of their greater <a href="/wiki/Fertility" title="Fertility">fertility</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rates</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Neo-malthusianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-malthusianism">Neo-Malthusians</a> have slightly modified this analysis by increasing their focus on <a href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">overconsumption</a> - nonetheless, eco-socialists find this attention inadequate. They point to the fact that Malthus did not thoroughly examine ecology and that <a href="/wiki/Garrett_Hardin" title="Garrett Hardin">Garrett Hardin</a>, a key Neo-Malthusian, suggested that further <a href="/wiki/Enclosure" title="Enclosure">enclosed</a> and privatised land, as opposed to <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a>, would solve the chief environmental problem, which Hardin labeled the '<a href="/wiki/Tragedy_of_the_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="Tragedy of the Commons">Tragedy of the Commons</a>'.<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_.22two_varieties_of_environmentalism.22">The "two varieties of environmentalism"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The &quot;two varieties of environmentalism&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ramachandra_Guha" title="Ramachandra Guha">Guha</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Martinez-Alier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Juan Martinez-Alier (page does not exist)">Martinez-Alier</a> attack the gulf between what they see as the two "varieties of <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a>" - the environmentalism of the <a href="/wiki/Global_North" class="mw-redirect" title="Global North">North</a>, an aesthetic environmentalism that is the privilege of wealthy people who no longer have basic material concerns, and the environmentalism of the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">South</a>, where people's local environment is a source of communal wealth and such issues are a question of survival.<sup id="cite_ref-Guha_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guha-12">[12]</a></sup> Nonetheless, other eco-socialists, such as <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a>, have also pointed out that capitalism disproportionately affects the poorest in the Global North as well, leading to examples of resistance such as the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_justice" title="Environmental justice">environmental justice</a> movement in the US and groups like <a href="/wiki/MOVE" title="MOVE">MOVE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_other_forms_of_socialism">Critique of other forms of socialism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Critique of other forms of socialism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eco-socialists choose to use the term '<a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a>', despite "the failings of its twentieth century interpretations", because it "still stands for the supersession of <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capital</a>" and thus "the name, and the reality" must "become adequate for this time".<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Eco-socialists have nonetheless often diverged with other <a href="/wiki/Marxist" class="mw-redirect" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> movements. Eco-socialism has also been partly influenced by and associated with <a href="/wiki/Agrarian_socialism" title="Agrarian socialism">agrarian socialism</a> as well as some forms of <a href="/wiki/Christian_socialism" title="Christian socialism">Christian socialism</a>, especially in the United States.</p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_.27Actually_Existing_Socialisms.27">Critique of 'Actually Existing Socialisms'</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Critique of 'Actually Existing Socialisms'">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For Kovel and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Lowy" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Lowy">Lowy</a>, eco-socialism is "the realization of the “first-epoch” socialisms" by resurrecting the notion of "free development of all producers", distancing themselves from "the attenuated, reformist aims of <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democracy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Productivism" title="Productivism">productivist</a> structures of the <a href="/wiki/Bureaucratic_collectivism" title="Bureaucratic collectivism">bureaucratic variations</a> of socialism", such as forms of <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">Leninism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They ground the failure of past <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a> movements in "underdevelopment in the context of hostility by existing <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> powers", which led to "the denial of internal democracy" and "emulation of capitalist <a href="/wiki/Productivism" title="Productivism">productivism</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kovel believes that the forms of 'actually existing socialism' consisted of "public ownership of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a>", rather than meeting "the true definition" of socialism as "a <a href="/wiki/Free_association_(communism_and_anarchism)" title="Free association (communism and anarchism)">free association of producers</a>", with the Party-State bureaucracy acting as the "alienating substitute 'public'".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In analysing the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution_of_1917" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revolution of 1917">Russian Revolution</a>, Kovel feels that "conspiratorial" revolutionary movements "cut off from the development of society" will "find society an inert mass requiring leadership from above". From this, he notes that the anti-democratic <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Tsarist</a> heritage meant that the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevism">Bolsheviks</a>, who were aided into power by <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War One</a>, were a minority who, when faced with a <a href="/wiki/Counter-revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Counter-revolution">counter-revolution</a> and invading <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> powers, continued "the extraordinary needs of '<a href="/wiki/War_communism" title="War communism">war communism</a>'", which "put the seal of <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a>" on the revolution; thus, for Kovel, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Trotsky</a> "resorted to terror", shut down the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">Soviets</a> (workers' councils) and emulated "capitalist efficiency and <a href="/wiki/Productivism" title="Productivism">productivism</a> as a means of survival", setting the stage for <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a>, in Kovel's eyes, came to oppose the nascent <a href="/wiki/Bolshevism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevism">Bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalism</a> and its champion <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Bogdanov" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksandr Bogdanov">Aleksandr Bogdanov</a>, who was later attacked for "idealism"; Kovel describes <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Lenin</a>'s philosophy as "a sharply dualistic <a href="/wiki/Materialism" title="Materialism">materialism</a>, rather similar to the <a href="/wiki/Cartesianism" title="Cartesianism">Cartesian</a> separation of matter and consciousness, and perfectly tooled... to the active working over of the dead, dull matter by the human hand", which led him to want to overcome Russian backwardness through rapid <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a>. This tendency was, according to Kovel, augmented by a desire to catch-up with the <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">West</a> and the "severe crisis" of the revolution's first years.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Furthermore, Kovel quotes <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Trotsky</a>, who believed in a <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communist</a> "superman" who would "learn how to move rivers and mountains".<sup id="cite_ref-Trotsky_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trotsky-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kovel believes that, in <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Stalin</a>'s "revolution from above" and mass terror in response to the early 1930s economic crisis, <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Trotsky</a>'s writings "were given official imprimatur", despite the fact that <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Trotsky</a> himself was eventually purged, as <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">Stalinism</a> attacked "the very notion of ecology... in addition to ecologies". Kovel adds that <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Stalin</a> "would win the gold medal for enmity to nature", and that, in the face of massive <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a>, the inflexible <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> bureaucracy became increasingly inefficient and unable to emulate capitalist accumulation, leading to a "vicious cycle" that led to its collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critique_of_the_wider_socialist_movement">Critique of the wider socialist movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Critique of the wider socialist movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beyond the forms of 'actually existing socialism', Kovel criticises <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialists</a> in general as treating ecology "as an afterthought" and holding "a naive faith in the ecological capacities of a <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> defined by generations of <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> production". He exemplifies <a href="/wiki/David_McNally_(professor)" title="David McNally (professor)">David McNally</a>, who advocated increasing consumption levels under socialism, which, for Kovel, contradicts any notion of natural limits. He also criticises McNally's belief in releasing the "positive side of <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capital</a>'s self-expansion"<sup id="cite_ref-McNally_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNally-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> after the emancipation of labor; instead, Kovel argues that a <a href="/wiki/Socialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist">socialist</a> society would "seek not to become larger" but would rather become "more <i>realized</i>", choosing sufficiency and eschewing <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>. Kovel further adds that the <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> movement was historically conditioned by its origins in the era of <a href="/wiki/Industrialization" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> so that, when modern <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialists</a> like <a href="/wiki/David_McNally_(professor)" title="David McNally (professor)">McNally</a> advocate a socialism that "cannot be at the expense of the range of human satisfaction",<sup id="cite_ref-McNally_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNally-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> they fail "to recognize that these satisfactions can be problematic with respect to nature when they have been historically shaped by the domination of nature".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Eco-socialist_strategy">Eco-socialist strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Eco-socialist strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Eco-socialists generally advocate the <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">non-violent</a> dismantling of capitalism and the state, focusing on collective ownership of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> by freely associated producers and restoration of the <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">Commons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Manifesto_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manifesto-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> To get to an eco-socialist society, eco-socialists advocate <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a> resistance but also believe that there is potential for agency in autonomous, grassroots individuals and groups across the world who can build "prefigurative" projects for <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">non-violent</a> radical social change.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>These prefigurative steps go "beyond the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a> and the state"<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup> and base production on the enhancement of <a href="/wiki/Use_value" title="Use value">use values</a>, leading to the internationalization of resistance communities in an 'Eco-socialist Party' or network of grassroots groups focused on <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">non-violent</a>, radical social transformation. An 'Eco-socialist revolution' is then carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <small><i>(May 2013)</i></small></span></td>
