<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agency">Agency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Agency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many eco-socialists, like Alan Roberts, have encouraged <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> action and resistance, such as the '<a href="/wiki/Green_ban" title="Green ban">green ban</a>' movement in which workers refuse to participate in projects that are ecologically harmful.<sup id="cite_ref-Roberts_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roberts-44">[44]</a></sup> Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> focuses on <a href="/wiki/Working-class" class="mw-redirect" title="Working-class">working-class</a> involvement in the formation of eco-socialist parties or their increased involvement in existing <a href="/wiki/Green_Parties" class="mw-redirect" title="Green Parties">Green Parties</a>; however, he believes that, unlike many other forms of <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> analysis, "there is no privileged agent" or revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">class</a>, and that there is potential for agency in numerous autonomous, grassroots individuals and groups who can build "prefigurative" projects for <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">non-violent</a> radical social change. He defines "prefiguration" as "the potential for the given to contain the lineaments of what is to be", meaning that "a moment toward the future exists embedded in every point of the social organism where a need arises".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>If "everything has prefigurative potential", Kovel notes that forms of potential <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> production will be "scattered", and thus suggests that "the task is to free them and connect them". While all "human <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>" have "ecosocialist potential", Kovel points out that ones such as the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> have low potential, whereas internally democratic <a href="/wiki/Anti-globalization" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-globalization">anti-globalization</a> "affinity groups" have a high potential through a dialectic that involves the "active bringing and holding together of negations", such as the group acting as an alternative institution ("production of an <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a>/<a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> alternative") and trying to shut down a <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">G8</a> summit meeting ("resistance to capital"). Therefore, "practices that in the same motion enhance <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a> and diminish <a href="/wiki/Exchange-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Exchange-value">exchange-values</a> are the ideal" for eco-socialists.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prefiguration">Prefiguration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Prefiguration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For Kovel, the main prefigurative steps "are that people ruthlessly criticize the capitalist system... and that they include in this a consistent attack on the widespread belief that there can be no alternative to it", which will then "deligitimate the system and release people into struggle". Kovel justifies this by stating that "radical criticism of the given... can be a material force", even without an alternative, "because it can seize the mind of the masses of people", leading to "dynamic" and "exponential", rather than "incremental" and "linear", victories that spread rapidly. Following this, he advocates the expansion of the dialectical eco-socialist potential of groups through sustaining the confrontation and internal cohesion of <a href="/wiki/Human_ecosystem" title="Human ecosystem">human ecosystems</a>, leading to an "activation" of potentials in others that will "spread across the whole social field" as "a new set of orienting principles" that define an ideology or "'party-life' formation".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the short-term, eco-socialists like Kovel advocate activities that have the "promise of breaking down the commodity form". This includes organizing labor, which is a "reconfiguring of the <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-value</a> of labor power"; forming <a href="/wiki/Cooperatives" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperatives">cooperatives</a>, allowing "a relatively free association of labor"; forming localised currencies, which he sees as "undercutting the value-basis of money"; and supporting "radical media" that, in his eyes, involve an "undoing of the fetishism of commodities". <a href="/wiki/Arran_Gare" title="Arran Gare">Arran Gare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a> and Kovel have advocated economic <a href="/wiki/Localism_(politics)" title="Localism (politics)">localisation</a> in the same vein as many in the <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green movement</a>, although they stress that it must be a prefigurative step rather than an end in itself.<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gare2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gare2-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kovel also advises political parties attempting to "democratize the state" that there should be "dialogue but no compromise" with established political parties, and that there must be "a continual association of electoral work with movement work" to avoid "being sucked back into the system". Such parties, he believes, should focus on "the local rungs of the political system" first, before running national campaigns that "challenge the existing system by the elementary means of exposing its broken promises".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kovel believes in building prefigurations around forms of production based on <a href="/wiki/Use_value" title="Use value">use values</a>, which will provide a practical vision of a <a href="/wiki/Post-capitalism" title="Post-capitalism">post-capitalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-statism" title="Anti-statism">post-statist</a> system. Such projects include <a href="/wiki/Indymedia" class="mw-redirect" title="Indymedia">Indymedia</a> ("a democratic rendering of the <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a> of new technologies such as the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>, and a continual involvement in wider struggle"), <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-source software</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_libraries" class="mw-redirect" title="Public libraries">public libraries</a> and many other initiatives, especially those developed within the <a href="/wiki/Anti-globalisation_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-globalisation movement">anti-globalisation movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These strategies, in <a href="/wiki/Derek_Wall" title="Derek Wall">Wall</a>'s words, "go beyond the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a> and the state" by rejecting the supposed dichotomy between <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">private enterprise</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Government-owned corporation">state-owned</a> production, while also rejecting any combination of the two through a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a>. He states that these present forms of "amphibious politics", which are "half in the dirty water of the present but seeking to move on to a new, unexplored territory".<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Wall suggests that <a href="/wiki/Open_source_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source software">open source software</a>, for example, opens up "a new form of <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a> regime in <a href="/wiki/Cyberspace" title="Cyberspace">cyberspace</a>", which he praises as production "for the pleasure of invention" that gives "access to resources without exchange". He believes that <a href="/wiki/Open_source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source">open source</a> has "bypassed" both the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a> and the state, and could provide "developing countries with free access to vital computer software". Furthermore, he suggests that an "<a href="/wiki/Open_source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source">open source</a> economy" means that "the barrier between user and provider is eroded", allowing for "cooperative creativity". He links this to <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> and the notion of <a href="/wiki/Usufruct" title="Usufruct">usufruct</a>, asserting that "Marx would have been a <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a> user".<sup id="cite_ref-Babylon_20-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babylon-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internationalization_of_prefiguration_and_the_.27Eco-socialist_Party.27">Internationalization of prefiguration and the 'Eco-socialist Party'</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Internationalization of prefiguration and the 'Eco-socialist Party'">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many eco-socialists have noted that the potential for building such projects is easier for media workers than for those in heavy industry because of the decline in <a href="/wiki/Trade_unionism" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade unionism">trade unionism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalized</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_of_labor" class="mw-redirect" title="Division of labor">division of labor</a> which divides workers. However, Kovel believes that examples like the <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> <a href="/wiki/Bruderhof_Communities" title="Bruderhof Communities">Bruderhof Communities</a> (despite elements of <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchy</a> that he attacks) show that "communistic" organizations can "survive rather well in a heavily industrialized <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a>" if they are "protected" from the dependence on the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a> by "<a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalist</a> intentionality". He further posits that <a href="/wiki/Class_struggle" class="mw-redirect" title="Class struggle">class struggle</a> is "internationalized in the face of globalization", as evidenced by a wave of <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">strikes</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a> in the first half of the year 2000; indeed, he says that "labor's most cherished values are already immanently ecocentric".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Kovel therefore thinks that these universalizing tendencies must lead to the formation of "a consciously 'Ecosocialist Party'" that is neither like a parliamentary or vanguardist party. Instead, Kovel advocates a form of <a href="/wiki/Political_party" title="Political party">political party</a> "grounded in communities of resistance", where delegates from these communities form the core of the party's activists, and these delegates and the "open and transparent" assembly they form are subject to <a href="/wiki/Recall_election" title="Recall election">recall</a> and regular rotation of members. He holds up the <a href="/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation" title="Zapatista Army of National Liberation">Zapatista Army of National Liberation</a> (EZLN) and the <a href="/wiki/Gaviotas" title="Gaviotas">Gaviotas</a> movement as examples of such communities, which "are produced outside capitalist circuits" and show that "there can be no single way valid for all peoples".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Nonetheless, he also firmly believes in connecting these movements, stating that "ecosocialism will be international or it will be nothing" and hoping that the Ecosocialist Party can retain the autonomy of local communities while supporting them materially. With an ever-expanding party, Kovel hopes that "defections" by <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalists</a> will occur, leading eventually to the <a href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">police</a> who, in joining the <a href="/wiki/Revolution" title="Revolution">revolution</a>, will signify that "the turning point is reached".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id=".27The_Revolution.27_and_transition_to_eco-socialism">'The Revolution' and transition to eco-socialism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 'The Revolution' and transition to eco-socialism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a single <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">source</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Eco-socialism#.23" title="Talk:Eco-socialism">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <small><i>(May 2013)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>'The Revolution' as envisaged by eco-socialists involves an immediate socio-political transition. Internationally, eco-socialists believe in a reform of the nature of <a href="/wiki/Money" title="Money">money</a> and the formation of a 'World People's Trade Organisation' (WPTO) that democratizes and improves world <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a> through the calculation of an 'Ecological Price' (EP) for goods. This would then be followed by a transformation of socioeconomic conditions towards ecological production, <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a> land and notions of <a href="/wiki/Usufruct" title="Usufruct">usufruct</a> (that seek to improve the common property possessed by society) to end private <a href="/wiki/Property" title="Property">property</a>. Eco-socialists assert that this must be carried out with adherence to <a href="/wiki/Non-violence" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-violence">non-violence</a><sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_immediate_aftermath_of_the_revolution">The immediate aftermath of the revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: The immediate aftermath of the revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eco-socialists like <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a> use the term "Eco-socialist revolution" to describe the transition to an eco-socialist world society. In the immediate socio-political transition, he believes that four groups will emerge from the revolution – revolutionaries, those "whose productive activity is directly compatible with ecological production" (such as nurses, schoolteachers, librarians, independent farmers and many other examples), those "whose pre-revolutionary practice was given over to <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capital</a>" (including the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeoisie</a>, advertising executives and more) and "the workers whose activity added surplus value to capitalist commodities".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In terms of political organisation, he advocates an "interim assembly" made up of the revolutionaries that can "devise incentives to make sure that vital functions are maintained" (such as short-term continuation of "differential remuneration" for labor), "handle the redistribution of social roles and assets", convene "in widespread locations", and send delegates to regional, state, national and international organisations, where every level has an "executive council" that is rotated and can be recalled. From there, he asserts that "productive communities" will "form the political as well as economic unit of society" and "organize others" to make a transition to eco-socialist production.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>He adds that people will be allowed to be members of any community they choose with "associate membership" of others, such as a <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">doctor</a> having main membership of healthcare communities as a <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">doctor</a> and associate membership of child-rearing communities as a father. Each locality would, in Kovel’s eyes, require one community that administered the areas of jurisdiction through an elected assembly. High-level assemblies would have additional "supervisory" roles over localities to monitor the development of <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystemic</a> integrity, and administer "society-wide services" like transport in "state-like functions", before the interim assembly can transfer responsibilities to "the level of the society as a whole through appropriate and democratically responsive committees".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transnational_trade_and_capital_reform">Transnational trade and capital reform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transnational trade and capital reform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Part of the eco-socialist transition, in Kovel’s eyes, is the reforming <a href="/wiki/Money" title="Money">money</a> to retain its use in "enabling exchanges" while reducing its functions as "a commodity in its own right" and "repository of value". He argues for directing <a href="/wiki/Money" title="Money">money</a> to "enhancement of <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a>" through a "subsidization of <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a>" that "preserves the functioning core of the economy while gaining time and space for rebuilding it". Internationally, he believes in the immediate cessation of <a href="/wiki/Speculation" title="Speculation">speculation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currencies</a> ("breaking down the function of money as commodity, and redirecting funds on <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a>"), the cancellation of the debt of the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">Global South</a> ("breaking the back of the value function" of money) and the redirecting the "vast reservoir of mainly phony value" to reparations and "ecologically sound development". He suggests the end of military aid and other forms of support to "<a href="/w/index.php?title=Comprador_elites&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Comprador elites (page does not exist)">comprador elites</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Global_South" title="Global South">South</a>" will eventually "lead to their collapse".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In terms of <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a>, Kovel advocates a ‘World People’s Trade Organization’ (WPTO), "responsible to a confederation of popular bodies", in which "the degree of control over <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trade</a> is... proportional to involvement with production", meaning that "farmers would have a special say over food trade" and so on. He posits that the WPTO should have an elected council that will oversee a reform of prices in favour of an ‘Ecological Price’ (EP) "determined by the difference between actual <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a> and fully realized ones", thus having low <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> for forms of ecological production like <a href="/wiki/Organic_agriculture" class="mw-redirect" title="Organic agriculture">organic agriculture</a>; he also envisages the high <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> on non-ecological production providing subsidies to ecological production units.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The EP would also internalize the costs of current <a href="/wiki/Externality" title="Externality">externalities</a> (like <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a>) and "would be set as a function of the distance traded", reducing the effects of long-distance transport like <a href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> and increased <a href="/wiki/Packaging" class="mw-redirect" title="Packaging">packaging</a> of goods. He thinks that this will provide a "standard of transformation" for non-ecological industries, like the <a href="/wiki/Automobile_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Automobile industry">automobile industry</a>, thus spurring changes towards ecological production.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_production">Ecological production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Ecological production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eco-socialists pursue "<a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> production" that, according to <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a>, goes beyond the <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> vision of the emancipation of labor to "the realization of <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-values</a> and the appropriation of intrinsic value". He envisions a form of production in which "the making of a thing becomes part of the thing made" so that, using a high quality meal as an analogy, "pleasure would obtain for the cooking of the meal" - thus activities "reserved as hobbies under capitalism" would "compose the fabric of everyday life" under eco-socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>This, for Kovel, is achieved if labor is "freely chosen and developed... with a fully realized <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-value</a>" achieved by a "negation" of <a href="/wiki/Exchange-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Exchange-value">exchange-value</a>, and he exemplifies the <a href="/wiki/Food_Not_Bombs" title="Food Not Bombs">Food Not Bombs</a> project for adopting this. He believes that the notion of "mutual recognition... for the process as well as the product" will avoid <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour" title="Exploitation of labour">exploitation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy" title="Hierarchy">hierarchy</a>. With production allowing humanity to "live more directly and receptively embedded in <a href="/wiki/Nature" title="Nature">nature</a>", Kovel predicts that "a reorientation of human need" will occur that recognises <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> limits and sees <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a> as "fully participant in the life of <a href="/wiki/Eco-system" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-system">eco-systems</a>", thus removing it from profit-making exercises.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the course on an Eco-socialist revolution, writers like Kovel advocate the a "rapid conversion to ecosocialist production" for all enterprises, followed by "restoring <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystemic</a> integrity to the workplace" through steps like workers ownership. He then believes that the new enterprises can build "socially developed plans" of production for societal needs, such as efficient light-rail transport components. At the same time, Kovel argues for the transformation of essential but, under capitalism, non-productive labour, such as child care, into productive labour, "thereby giving reproductive labour a status equivalent to productive labour".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>During such a transition, he believes that income should be guaranteed and that money will still be used under "new conditions of value… according to use and to the degree to which ecosystem integrity is developed and advanced by any particular production". Within this structure, Kovel asserts that markets and will become unnecessary – although "market phenomena" in personal exchanges and other small instances might be adopted – and communities and elected assemblies will democratically decide on the allocation of resources.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_M%C3%A9sz%C3%A1ros_(professor)" title="István Mészáros (professor)">Istvan Meszaros</a> believes that such "genuinely planned and self-managed (as opposed to bureaucratically planned from above) productive activities" are essential if eco-socialism is to meet its "fundamental objectives".<sup id="cite_ref-Meszaros_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meszaros-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eco-socialists are quick to assert that their focus on "production" does not mean that there will be an increase in production and labor under Eco-socialism. Kovel thinks that the emancipation of labor and the realization of <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-value</a> will allow "the spheres of work and culture to be reintegrated". He cites the example of <a href="/wiki/Guarani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Guarani people">Paraguayan Indian</a> communities (organised by <a href="/wiki/Jesuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a>) in the eighteenth century who made sure that all community members learned musical instruments, and had labourers take musical instruments to the fields and takes turns playing music or harvesting.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commons.2C_property_and_.27usufruct.27">Commons, property and 'usufruct'</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Commons, property and 'usufruct'">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most eco-socialists, including <a href="/wiki/Ramachandra_Guha" title="Ramachandra Guha">Guha</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Martinez-Alier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Juan Martinez-Alier (page does not exist)">Martinez-Alier</a>, echo subsistence <a href="/wiki/Eco-feminism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-feminism">eco-feminists</a> like <a href="/wiki/Vandana_Shiva" title="Vandana Shiva">Vandana Shiva</a> when they argue for the restoration of <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a> land over <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a>. They blame <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> degradation on the inclination to short-term, profit-inspired decisions inherent within a <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a> system. For them, <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatization</a> of land strips people of their local communal resources in the name of creating markets for <a href="/wiki/Neo-liberalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-liberalism">neo-liberal globalisation</a>, which benefits a minority. In their view, successful <a href="/wiki/Commons" title="Commons">commons</a> systems have been set up around the world throughout history to manage areas cooperatively, based on long-term needs and <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> instead of short-term profit.<sup id="cite_ref-Guha_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guha-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many eco-socialists focus on a modified version of the notion of ‘<a href="/wiki/Usufruct" title="Usufruct">Usufruct</a>’ to replace capitalist private <a href="/wiki/Property" title="Property">property</a> arrangements. As a legal term, <a href="/wiki/Usufruct" title="Usufruct">Usufruct</a> refers to the legal right to use and derive profit or benefit from <a href="/wiki/Property" title="Property">property</a> that belongs to another person, as long as the property is not damaged. According to eco-socialists like Kovel, a modern interpretation of the idea is "where one uses, enjoys – and through that, improves – another’s property", as its <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> etymology "condenses the two meanings of use – as in <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-value</a>, and enjoyment – and as in the gratification expressed in freely associated labour". The idea, according to Kovel, has roots in the <a href="/wiki/Code_of_Hammurabi" title="Code of Hammurabi">Code of Hammurabi</a> and was first mentioned in <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> "where it applied to ambiguities between masters and slaves with respect to property"; it also features in <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia law</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Aztecz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aztecz (page does not exist)">Aztec</a> law and the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Crucially for eco-socialists, Marx mentioned the idea when he stated that human beings are no more than the planet’s "<a href="/wiki/Usufruct" title="Usufruct">usufructaries</a>, and, like <i>boni patres familias</i>, they must hand it down to succeeding generations in an improved condition".<sup id="cite_ref-Capital3_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capital3-19">[19]</a></sup> Kovel and others have taken on this reading, asserting that, in an eco-socialist society, "everyone will have... rights of use and ownership over those means of production necessary to express the creativity of human nature", namely "a place of one’s own" to decorate to personal taste, some personal possessions, the body and its attendant sexual and <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_rights" title="Reproductive rights">reproductive rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>However, Kovel sees <a href="/wiki/Property" title="Property">property</a> as "self-contradictory" because individuals emerge "in a tissue of social relations" and "nested circles", with the self at the centre and extended circles where "issues of sharing arise from early childhood on". He believes that "the full self is enhanced more by giving than by taking" and that eco-socialism is realized when material possessions weigh "lightly" upon the self – thus restoration of <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-value</a> allows things to be taken "concretely and sensuously" but "lightly, since things are enjoyed for themselves and not as buttresses for a shaky ego".<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>This, for Kovel, reverses what Marxists see as the <a href="/wiki/Commodity_fetishism" title="Commodity fetishism">commodity fetishism</a> and atomization of individuals (through the "unappeasable craving" for "having and excluding others from having") under capitalism. Under eco-socialism, he therefore believes that enhancement of <a href="/wiki/Use-value" class="mw-redirect" title="Use-value">use-value</a> will lead to differentiated ownership between the individual and the collective, where there are "distinct limits on the amount of <a href="/wiki/Property" title="Property">property</a> individuals control" and no-one can take control of resources that "would permit the alienation of <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> from another". He then hopes that the "hubris" of the notion of "ownership of the planet" will be replaced with <a href="/wiki/Usufruct" title="Usufruct">usufruct</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-violence">Non-violence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Non-violence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most eco-socialists are involved in peace and antiwar movements, and eco-socialist writers, like <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel</a>, generally believe that "violence is the rupturing of <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>" and is therefore "deeply contrary to ecosocialist values". Kovel believes that revolutionary movements must prepare for post-revolutionary violence from counter-revolutionary sources by "prior development of the democratic sphere" within the movement, because "to the degree that people are capable of self-government, so will they turn away from violence and retribution" for "a self-governed people cannot be pushed around by any alien government". It is therefore essential, in <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Kovel's</a> view, that the revolution "takes place in" or spreads quickly to the United States, which "is capital's gendarme and will crush any serious threat", and that revolutionaries reject the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a> and retribution against former opponents or counter-revolutionaries.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms_of_eco-socialism">Criticisms of eco-socialism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Criticisms of eco-socialism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>While in many ways the criticisms of eco-socialism combine the traditional criticisms of both socialism and Green politics, there are unique critiques of eco-socialism, which are largely from within the traditional <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">Socialist</a> or <a href="/wiki/Green_politics" title="Green politics">Green movements</a> themselves, along with <a href="/wiki/Conservativism" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservativism">conservative</a> criticisms.</p>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialists</a> are critical of the word 'eco-socialism'. <a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Reilly_(Eco-socialist)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="David Reilly (Eco-socialist) (page does not exist)">David Reilly</a>, who questions whether his argument is improved by the use of an "exotic word", argues instead that the "real socialism" is "also a green or 'eco'" one that you get to "by dint of struggle".<sup id="cite_ref-LeftClickCritic_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeftClickCritic-74">[74]</a></sup> Other socialists, like <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hampton" title="Paul Hampton">Paul Hampton</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Workers%27_Liberty" title="Alliance for Workers' Liberty">Alliance for Workers' Liberty</a> (a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Third_camp" title="Third camp">third camp socialist</a> party), see eco-socialism as "classless ecology", wherein eco-socialists have "given up on the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a>" as the privileged agent of struggle by "borrowing bits from Marx but missing the locus of Marxist politics".<sup id="cite_ref-AWLCritic_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWLCritic-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Writing in <i><a href="/wiki/Capitalism_Nature_Socialism" title="Capitalism Nature Socialism">Capitalism Nature Socialism</a></i>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Doug_Boucher&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Doug Boucher (page does not exist)">Doug Boucher</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peter_Caplan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peter Caplan (page does not exist)">Peter Caplan</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Schwartzman" title="David Schwartzman">David Schwartzman</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jane_Zara&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jane Zara (page does not exist)">Jane Zara</a> criticise eco-socialists in general (and <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Joel Kovel</a> in particular) for a deterministic "<a href="/wiki/Catastrophism" title="Catastrophism">catastrophism</a>" that overlooks "the countervailing tendencies of both popular struggles and the efforts of capitalist governments to rationalize the system" and the "accomplishments of the <a href="/wiki/Labor_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Labor movement">labor movement</a>" that "demonstrate that despite the interests and desires of capitalists, progress toward <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a> is possible". They argue that an ecological socialism must be "built on hope, not fear".<sup id="cite_ref-CNSCritics_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNSCritics-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">Conservatives</a> have criticised the perceived opportunism of <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing</a> groups who have increased their focus on green issues since the fall of <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fred_L._Smith_(political_writer)" title="Fred L. Smith (political writer)">Fred L. Smith</a> Jr., President of the <a href="/wiki/Competitive_Enterprise_Institute" title="Competitive Enterprise Institute">Competitive Enterprise Institute</a> think-tank, exemplifies the conservative critique of left Greens, attacking the "<a href="/wiki/Pantheism" title="Pantheism">pantheism</a>" of the Green movement and conflating "<a href="/wiki/Neopaganism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neopaganism">eco-paganism</a>" with eco-socialism. Like many conservative critics, Smith uses the term 'eco-socialism' to attack non-socialist <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalists</a> for advocating restrictions on the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a>, although he does recognise and condemn the influence of socialist ideals on many in the Green movement who reject <a href="/wiki/Private_property" title="Private property">private property</a>, and instead advocates <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">market</a>-based solutions to ecological problems. He nevertheless wrongly claims that eco-socialists endorse "the <a href="/wiki/Malthusianism" title="Malthusianism">Malthusian</a> view of the relationship between man and nature", and states that <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a> and now a <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> campaigner, is an eco-socialist, despite the fact that <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Gore</a> has never used this term and is not recognised as a such by other followers of either Green politics or socialism.<sup id="cite_ref-SmithCritic_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SmithCritic-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmentalists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conservation_movement" title="Conservation movement">conservationists</a> have criticised eco-socialism from within the Green movement. In a review of <a href="/wiki/Joel_Kovel" title="Joel Kovel">Joel Kovel</a>'s <i>The Enemy of Nature</i>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=David_M._Johns&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="David M. Johns (page does not exist)">David M. Johns</a> criticises eco-socialism for not offering "suggestions about near term <a href="/wiki/Conservation_movement" title="Conservation movement">conservation</a> policy" and focusing exclusively on long-term societal transformation. Johns believes that <a href="/wiki/Species_extinction" class="mw-redirect" title="Species extinction">species extinction</a> "started much earlier" than capitalism and suggests that eco-socialism neglects the fact that an <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecological</a> society will need to transcend the destructiveness found in "all large-scale societies".<sup id="cite_ref-NPSCritic_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPSCritic-78">[78]</a></sup> the very tendency that Kovel himself attacks among capitalists and traditional leftists who attempt to reduce nature to "linear" human models.<sup id="cite_ref-Kovel_13-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kovel-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (June 2014)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Johns questions whether non-hierarchical social systems can provide for billions of people, and criticises eco-socialists for neglecting issues of <a href="/wiki/Over-population" class="mw-redirect" title="Over-population">population pressure</a>. Furthermore, Johns describes Kovel's argument that human hierarchy is founded on raiding to steal women as "archaic".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_eco-socialists">List of eco-socialists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eco-socialism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: List of eco-socialists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Elmar_Altvater" title="Elmar Altvater">Elmar Altvater</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ian_Angus_(activist)" title="Ian Angus (activist)">Ian Angus</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rudolph_Bahro" class="mw-redirect" title="Rudolph Bahro">Rudolph Bahro</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Bellamy_Foster" title="John Bellamy Foster">John Bellamy Foster</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Murray_Bookchin" title="Murray Bookchin">Murray Bookchin</a></li>

<li id="cite_note-Thoreau-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Thoreau_23-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Su obra más representativa es Walden, aparecida en 1854, aunque redactada entre 1845 y 1847, cuando Thoreau decide instalarse en el aislamiento de una cabaña en el bosque, y vivir en íntimo contacto con la naturaleza, en una vida de soledad y sobriedad. De esta experiencia, su filosofía trata de transmitirnos la idea que resulta necesario un retorno respetuoso a la naturaleza, y que la felicidad es sobre todo fruto de la riqueza interior y de la armonía de los individuos con el entorno natural. Muchos han visto en Thoreau a uno de los precursores del ecologismo y del anarquismo primitivista representado en la actualidad por <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a>. Para George Woodcock, esta actitud puede estar también motivada por una cierta idea de resistencia al progreso y de rechazo al materialismo creciente que caracteriza la sociedad norteamericana de mediados de siglo XIX."<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.acracia.org/xdiez.html">"LA INSUMISIÓN VOLUNTARIA. EL ANARQUISMO INDIVIDUALISTA ESPAÑOL DURANTE LA DICTADURA Y LA SEGUNDA REPÚBLICA (1923-1938)" by Xavier Diez</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060526224800/http://www.acracia.org/xdiez.html">Archived</a> 26 May 2006 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.</span></li>

<li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-66">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, Scottish Green Peter McColl argues that elected governments should abolish poverty through a Citizens Income scheme, regulate against social and environmental malpractice and encourage environmental good practice through state procurement. At the same time economic and political power should be devolved as far as is possible through co-operatives, and increased local decision making. By putting political and economic power into the hands of the people most likely to be affected by environmental injustice it is less likely that the injustice will take place - see <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.redflag.org.uk/frontline/frJune08/ecosoc2.html">http://www.redflag.org.uk/frontline/frJune08/ecosoc2.html</a></span></li>
